<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

	<div class="pure-g">
		<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage --><div ng-if="::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage" ng-class="vm.details.graphicalAbstract ? 			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">In this paper, a horizontally meandered strip (HMS) feed technique is proposed to achieve good impedance matching and symmetrical broadside radiation patterns for a single-fed broadband circularly polarized stacked patch antenna, which is suitable for universal ultrahigh frequency (UHF) RF identification (RFID) applications. The antenna is composed of two corner truncated patches and an HMS, all of which are printed on the upper side of the FR4 substrates. One end of the HMS is connected to the main patch by a probe, while the other end is connected to an SMA connector. Simulation results are compared with the measurements, and a good agreement is obtained. The measurements show that the antenna has an impedance bandwidth (VSWR &lt;; 1.5) of about 25.8% (758-983 MHz), a 3-dB axial ratio (AR) bandwidth of about 13.5% (838-959 MHz), and a gain level of about 8.6 dBic or larger within the 3-dB AR bandwidth. Therefore, the proposed antenna can be a good candidate for universal UHF RFID readers operating at the UHF band of 840-955 MHz. In addition, a parametric study and a design guideline of the proposed antenna are presented to provide the engineers with information for designing, modifying, and optimizing such an antenna. At last, the proposed antenna is validated in RFID system applications.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Rf identification (rfid) is the use of a tag applied to or incorporated into a product, animal, or person for the purpose of identification and tracking by radio waves, which can be traced back to World War II. It is already widely used in animal tagging, supply chain management, and electronic payment, such as the Public Transportation Card. Currently, many other potential applications in the Internet of Things (IOT), a vision in which the Internet extends into our everyday lives through a wireless network of uniquely identifiable objects, are being investigated <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. In this regard, passive RFID systems operating at ultrahigh frequency (UHF) are anticipated as being the most practical as they offer a good balance between range (typically less than a few meters) and the ability to read multiple tags at speed. However, the UHF frequencies authorized for RFID applications are different in different countries and regions <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. Most countries allocate UHF frequencies within the band from 865 to 928 MHz, except Chinese 840.5â844.5 MHz and Japanese 952â955 MHz. In view of this, an RFID system operating the entire UHF RFID frequency band of 840â955 MHz (a fractional bandwidth of 12.8%) would be beneficial for system implementation and cost reduction. The RFID system consists of the reader and the tag. Since the RFID tags may be arbitrarily positioned and the tag antennas are normally linearly polarized, circularly polarized (CP) antennas are used in UHF RFID readers for ensuring the reliability of communications between readers and tags <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. Many types of antennas can generate CP radiation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>, wherein a patch antenna is one of the most commonly used. In general, the feed structures of CP patch antennas can be categorized into single and dual feeds.</p><p>On the one hand, for the single-fed technique, asymmetry is introduced into the geometry of the patches so that when the antenna is excited at a carefully selected feed point, the antenna radiates a CP wave. Thus, a single-fed CP patch antenna has the advantages of simple structure, easy manufacture, and low cost. However, the single-fed single-patch CP antenna suffers from inherent narrow impedance and axial ratio (AR) bandwidth, typically less than 2% <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>. For a better bandwidth, the patch antenna is usually designed to have thick air or foam substrates. The performance of single-fed single-patch CP antennas with different air-layer substrate thickness is reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a> and the AR bandwidth is enhanced to 14% when the substrate thickness is about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 2.526em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.285em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.28em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.2</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-4"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î»</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-7"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">o</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">0.2\lambda_{o}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. If the method is used to design a universal UHF RFID reader antenna, the antenna height will be greater than 60 mm <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-9" role="math" style="width: 4.027em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.607em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.49em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-11" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.18</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-13"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-14" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î»</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-16"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">o</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-18" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">(0.18\lambda_{o})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is not suitable for practical applications. In addition, impedance matching bandwidth cannot cover the 3-dB AR bandwidth when a thick air-layer substrate is used <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>. One technique for achieving a single-fed broadband CP patch antenna is the use of stacked elements. Herscovici et al. used a probe-fed rectangular patch with an almost square parasitic element to achieve an excellent AR bandwidth of 13% <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>. Their main patch is on a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-19" role="math" style="width: 3.667em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.306em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.31em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-20"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-21" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.041</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-22"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-23" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î»</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-24"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-25"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-26" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">o</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">0.041\lambda_{o}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> thick foam substrate and the total thickness of the antenna is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-27" role="math" style="width: 3.667em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.306em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.31em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-28"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-29" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.085</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-30"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-31" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î»</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-32"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-33"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-34" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">o</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">0.085\lambda_{o}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Considering that the patches on foam substrates are difficult to fabricate, the patches are printed on dielectric substrates, and 3-dB AR bandwidth of 14.8% <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a> or 18.8% <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a> have been achieved by optimizing the feed location or patch configuration. Nevertheless, the voltage standing-wave ratio (VSWR) of the antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a> is only less than 2 in the 3-dB AR band, which is not suitable for the RFID reader requiring good impedance matching <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-35" role="math" style="width: 7.21em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.489em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.37em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-36"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-37" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-38"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-39"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-40" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">V</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-41" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-42" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">W</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-43" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-44" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&lt;</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-45" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1.5</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-46" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">({\rm VSWR}&lt;1.5)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. As we known, using an aperture coupled feed <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a> or L-shaped strip feed <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a>, patch antennas have good impedance matching. However, the aperture coupled patch antenna needs a reflecting plate to block back radiation, which increases the complexity of the antenna configuration. In addition, the effects of the length of the vertical and horizontal portion of the L-shaped strip on input resistance and reactance are dependent, which result in a complex design process. By connecting the open end of the L-shaped strip to the patch, a modified L-strip feed structure is proposed <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_1">[16]</a>. We have proven the modified L-strip feed structure can easily determine input resistance and reactance, and achieved an impedance bandwidth of 22% for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-47" role="math" style="width: 6.369em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.709em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.65em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-48"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-49"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-50"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-51" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">V</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-52" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-53" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">W</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-54" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-55" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&lt;</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-56" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1.2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">{\rm VSWR}&lt;1.2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_1">[17]</a>. Nevertheless, it has disadvantages of having asymmetrical broadside radiation patterns and a very long horizontal strip extending outside the patch. The strip will make the projection area of the antenna too large for constructing antenna arrays.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5725144/5725144-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5725144/5725144-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 1. </b><fig><p>Geometry of the proposed patch antenna. (a) Top view. (b) Side view. (c) Front view.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5725144/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>On the other hand, for the dual-fed technique, two spatially orthogonal feeds are excited with a relative phase shift of 90Â°. The dual-fed method requires the use of a 90Â° hybrid or power splitter with unequal lengths of transmission line to provide the necessary phase shift. This approach generally features a wide AR bandwidth if both the radiator and feeding network are broadband, but suffers a complicated structure, increased antenna size, and expensive manufacture <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_1">[18]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_1">[19]</a>. It is important to note that a multifeed CP patch antenna is proposed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_1">[20]</a>, which has more complex antenna configuration. To reduce complexity of the multifeed CP patch antenna, three or four feeds of the patch are sequentially connected to the microstrip line and spatially positioned to achieve 90Â° phase difference between each feed point, and 3-dB AR bandwidth of 10.7% or 16.4% have been achieved, respectively <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_1">[21]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_1">[22]</a>. However, compared to the single-fed CP patch antenna, the design of the antennas is still complex. In addition, the two papers do not provide information on the feed process required to properly locate the feed point to achieve good circular polarization.</p><p>To obtain a simple and universal UHF RFID reader antenna, a single-fed broadband CP stacked patch antenna is proposed in this paper. The antenna is composed of two corner truncated patches and a horizontally meandered strip (HMS), all of which are printed on the upper side of the FR4 substrates. One end of the HMS is connected to the main patch by a probe, while the other end is connected to an SMA connector. The parasitic patch is positioned above the main patch for enhancing the bandwidth. The corners of the patches are truncated to obtain the CP radiation. The HMS feed technique is proposed to obtain good impedance matching and symmetrical broadside radiation patterns. The proposed antenna is designed to cover the entire UHF RFID band of 840â955 MHz with desired specifications such as good impedance matching, low AR, and high gain. Meanwhile, the antenna configuration is simple and easy for fabrication.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Antenna Structure and Implementation</h2></div><p>

The antenna is composed of two radiating patches, an HMS, a ground plane, an SMA connector, two probes, and three FR4 substrates. Air substrates are used in this configuration to achieve broader bandwidth, higher gain, and lower cost. The radiating patches and HMS are printed on the upper side of the three FR4 substrates, respectively. width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">S_{y}=19.6\ {\hbox{mm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the input resistance and reactance can be easily determined. The large inductance introduced by the long probe in the thick air-layer substrate is compensated by means of the electromagnetic coupling between the main patch and HMS. Basically, this simple and effective technique to broaden the impedance bandwidth is a similar to that of the design with the modified L-strip feed <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_2">[16]</a>, but the difference is that symmetrical broadside radiation pattern can be obtained by using the HMS. In order to obtain a symmetrical broadside radiation pattern from the patch antenna, it is found that this can be achieved by locating the HMS symmetrically with respect to the center of the patches. The symmetrical case is implemented by selecting <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-415" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.44em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-416"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-417"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-418" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-419"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-420"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-421"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-422"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-423" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-424" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">S_{{x}1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> equal to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-425" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.44em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-426"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-427"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-428" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-429"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-430"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-431"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-432"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-433" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-434" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">S_{{x}2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Furthermore, the length of the modified L-strip should be <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-435" role="math" style="width: 4.327em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.907em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.91em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-436"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-437" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â¼</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-438" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.47</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-439"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-440" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î»</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-441"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-442"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-443" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">\sim 0.47\lambda_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to obtain low cross-polarization levels of the linearly polarized patch antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_2">[16]</a>, but there is no limit to the length of the HMS for the CP patch antenna. This is because the size of the HMS has slight effects on the AR of the antenna. As a result, a wider impedance bandwidth and a more symmetrical radiation pattern for the patch antenna have been accomplished.</p><p>With aid of simulation by the Ansoft HFSS 3-D EM simulator <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_2">[23]</a>, which is based on the finite-element method (FEM), the antenna is optimized and then prototyped. The prototype in an anechoic chamber is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2(a)</a>. The radiating patches and HMS are etched on single-sided copper-clad FR4 laminates. The ground plane is made of copper, which is fixed with the FR4 laminates using plastic spacers. Copper wire is used as the probe to connect the main patch and the HMS. The inner conductor of an SMA connector is directly connected to the HMS and the outer conductor of that is soldered to the ground plane separately to simplify the implementation of the antenna.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Experimental Results and Analysis</h2></div><p>The prototype was measured in an anechoic chamber. The far-field performances were obtained using the SATIMO measurement system and the VSWR was measured by an Agilent E5071C vector network analyzer.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3(a)</a> shows the simulated and measured VSWR of the antenna. The measured VSWR is less than 1.5 over the frequency range of 758â983 MHz (25.8%), which can easily cover the entire UHF RFID frequency band of 840â955 MHz. A comparison between the simulated and measured AR at boresight is illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3(b)</a>. The measured 3-dB AR bandwidth of 838â959 MHz or 13.5% is obtained. The simulated and measured boresight gain is also displayed in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3(a)</a>. The antenna has a measured gain level of about 8.6 dBic or larger within the 3-dB AR bandwidth.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5725144/5725144-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5725144/5725144-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 3. </b><fig><p>Simulated and measured results of the proposed antenna. (a) VSWR and gain. (b) AR.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5725144/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a> shows the simulated and measured radiation patterns at 840, 900, and 955 MHz, respectively, in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-444" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-454"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-455" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-456"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-457"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-458"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-459"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-460" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">-</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-461" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">y{\hbox{-}}z</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-planes. It is observed that unlike other single-fed broadband CP patch antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_3">[24]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref25" id="context_ref_25_3">[25]</a>, the patch antenna with the proposed HMS has a more symmetrical radiation pattern across the operating bandwidth. There are many advantages if a CP patch antenna has a symmetrical radiation pattern. One advantage is that the maximum power direction would always be at the boresight direction and would not shift to different directions at different frequencies. Another advantage is that when constructing an antenna array, the radiation pattern would be more stable across the operating bandwidth. The two sidelobes of the 2 Ã 2 antenna array are different in magnitude <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_3">[26]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_3">[27]</a>. This is due to the fact that each antenna element has an unsymmetrical radiation pattern. It is also observed that the measured front-to-back ratio of the antenna is better than 16 dB at all measured frequencies. From the results in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 3</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">4</a>, the measured and simulated VSWR, AR, gain, and radiation patterns show good agreement.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5725144/5725144-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5725144/5725144-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 4. </b><fig><p>Simulated and measured radiation patterns of the proposed antenna. (a) 840 MHz. (b) 900 MHz. (c) 955 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5725144/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-510"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-511"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-512"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-513"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-514" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">-</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-515" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">y{\hbox{-}}z</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-planes.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TableÂ I </b>Summary of the Radiation Characteristics<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5725144/5725144-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5725144/5725144-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>

<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Parametric Studies and Design Guideline</h2></div><p>Parametric studies and a design guideline of the proposed antenna are presented to provide more detailed information about the antenna design and optimization. The parametric study is implemented by simulation because a good agreement between the simulation and measurement has been obtained. The performance of the proposed antenna is mainly determined by the characteristics of the HMS, feed probe, configuration of the patches including dimensions and heights, and size of the ground plane. Since the effects of the size and height of the main patch, size of the parasitic patch, size of the feed probe, and size of the ground plane, have been well known, the study of these parameters is excluded in this paper. The parameters under study focus on the truncation of the patches, height of the parasitic patch, position of the feed probe, size of the HMS, and plane reflector. To better understand the effect of the parameters on the performance of the antenna, only one parameter at a time will be varied, while the others are kept unchanged unless especially indicated.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Truncation of the Main Patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-516" role="math" style="width: 3.068em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.705em; height: 0px; font-size: 112%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.302em 1002.63em 2.601em -999.98em); top: -2.18em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-517"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-518" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-519" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-520"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.094em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.172em 1000.66em 4.159em -999.98em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-521" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.842em; left: 0.678em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-522"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-523"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-524" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-525" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.185em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.346em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.225em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">(\Delta L_{1})</script></tex-math></inline-formula></h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a> gives the effect of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-526" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-527"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-528" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-529"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-530" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-531"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-532"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-533" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">\Delta L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> on the AR and VSWR of the antenna. It is observed that the truncation of the main patch shows a significant effect on the AR of the antenna. The increasing of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-534" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-535"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-536" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-537"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-538" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-539"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-540"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-541" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">\Delta L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from 50 to 60 mm causes poorer impedance matching especially at lower band (near 810 MHz) and a narrow AR bandwidth. The decreasing of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-542" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-543"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-544" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-545"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-546" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-547"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-548"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-549" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">\Delta L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> improves AR bandwidth and achieves better impedance matching. However, over decreasing of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-550" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-551"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-552" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-553"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-554" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-555"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-556"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-557" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">\Delta L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (such as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-558" role="math" style="width: 6.91em; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-563"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-564"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-565" style="font-size: 70.7%; The gain of the antenna is modestly affected by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-574" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-575"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-576" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-577"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-578" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-579"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-580"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-581" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">\Delta L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and thus, the result is not illustrated. In practical design, the truncation can be optimized for specific design requirement.

<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Truncation of the Parasitic Patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-592" role="math" style="width: 3.068em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.705em; height: 0px; font-size: 112%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.302em 1002.63em 2.601em -999.98em); top: -2.18em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-593"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-594" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-595" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-596"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.094em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.172em 1000.66em 4.159em -999.98em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-597" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.842em; left: 0.678em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-598"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-599"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-600" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-601" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.185em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.346em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.225em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">(\Delta L_{2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula></h3><p>Compared to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-602" role="math" style="width: 4.748em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.267em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.27em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-603"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-604" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-605"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-606" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-607"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-608"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-609" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-610" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-611" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.183em;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-612"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-613" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-614"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-615"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-616" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">\Delta L_{1},\Delta L_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> has a lesser effect on the AR bandwidths. As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6</a>, when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-617" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-618"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-619" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-620"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-621" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-622"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-623"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-624" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">\Delta L_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is increased from 30 to 45 mm, the AR bandwidth of the antenna is gradually reduced. Similar to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-625" role="math" style="width: 4.748em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.267em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.27em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-626"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-627" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-628"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-629" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-630"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-631"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-632" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-633" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-634" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.183em;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-635"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-636" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-637"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-638"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-639" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">\Delta L_{1},\Delta L_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> also has a great effect on the impedance matching, but the worst appear at higher band (near 930 MHz). The gain of the antenna is also modestly affected by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-640" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-641"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-642" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-643"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-644" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-645"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-646"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-647" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">\Delta L_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5725144/5725144-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5725144/5725144-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 6. </b><fig><p>Effect of the truncation of the parasitic patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-648" role="math" style="width: 3.442em; <p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4c"><h3>C. Height of the Parasitic Patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-658" role="math" style="width: 1.977em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.769em; height: 0px; font-size: 112%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.302em 1001.7em 2.601em -999.98em); top: -2.18em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-659"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-660" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-661"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.99em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.172em 1000.56em 4.159em -999.98em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-662" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.842em; left: 0.574em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-663"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-664"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-665" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.004em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-666" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.185em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.346em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.225em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">(h_{2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula></h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a> shows the effect of varying height <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-667" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-668"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-669"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-670" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-671"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-672"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-673" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">h_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the parasitic patch on the AR of the antenna. When <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-674" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-675"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-676"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-677" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-678"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-679"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-680" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">h_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is increased from 12.0 to 16.5 mm, the AR of the antenna drops down, but the AR bandwidth is decreased. This is owing to the resonant frequency of the parasitic patch shifts down as the height increases. The decreasing of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-681" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-682"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-683"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-684" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-685"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-686"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-687" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">h_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can achieve better AR bandwidth. However, over decreasing of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-688" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-689"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-690"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-691" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-692"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-693"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-694" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">h_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (such as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-695" role="math" style="width: 6.73em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.069em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.07em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-696"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-697"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-698" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-699"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-700"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-701" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-702" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-703" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">10.5</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-704" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-705"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-706"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-707"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-708"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-709" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">h_{2}=10.5\ {\hbox{mm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) will degrade the AR bandwidth. In addition, when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-710" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-711"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-712"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-713" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-714"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-715"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-716" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">h_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is increased from 10.5 to 16.5 mm, the VSWR and gain of the antenna within the operating bandwidth is hardly affected so that the results are not presented.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5725144/5725144-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5725144/5725144-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 7. </b><fig><p>Effect of the height of the parasitic patch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-717" role="math" style="width: 2.186em; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-747" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">S_{{x}2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> on the input impedance and AR of the antenna with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-748" role="math" style="width: 4.748em; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-760" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-761"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-762"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-763"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-764"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-765" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-766" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">S_{{x}1}=S_{{x}2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It is found that the position of the feed probe has a significant effect on the input impedance. The input resistance and reactance decreases as the feed position moves inside the patch. This variation of input resistance is similar to that of the probe-fed patch antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4d">[28]</a>. The severe effect on input reactance is mainly because the length of the HMS varies as the position of the feed probe changes. Furthermore, the study shows that the position of the feed probe [shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8(b)</a>] and the size of the HMS have slight effects on the AR of the antenna. This means that the CP performance of the antenna mainly depends on the configuration of the patches. The feature makes the design of the proposed antenna simple and efficient.

<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4e"><h3>E. Size of the HMS (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-779" role="math" style="width: 1.198em;
